   <h1 class="firstHeading" id="firstHeading" lang="en">
    Decolonization
   </h1>
   <div class="mw-body-content" id="bodyContent">
    <div id="siteSub">
     From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia
    </div>
    <div id="contentSub">
    </div>
    <div class="mw-jump" id="jump-to-nav">
     Jump to:
     <a href="#mw-head">
      navigation
     </a>
     ,
     <a href="#p-search">
      search
     </a>
    </div>
    <div class="mw-content-ltr" dir="ltr" id="mw-content-text" lang="en">
     <p>
      <b>
       Decolonization
      </b>
      (
      <a href="/wiki/American_and_British_English_spelling_differences#-ise.2C_-ize_.28-isation.2C_-ization.29" title="American and British English spelling differences">
       US
      </a>
      ) or
      <b>
       decolonisation
      </b>
      (
      <a href="/wiki/American_and_British_English_spelling_differences#-ise.2C_-ize_.28-isation.2C_-ization.29" title="American and British English spelling differences">
       UK
      </a>
      ) is the undoing of
      <a href="/wiki/Colonialism" title="Colonialism">
       colonialism
      </a>
      , where a nation establishes and maintains its domination over dependent territories. The Oxford English Dictionary defines decolonization as "the withdrawal from its colonies of a colonial power; the acquisition of political or economic independence by such colonies."
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-1">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        1
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      It can be understood politically (attaining
      <a href="/wiki/Independence" title="Independence">
       independence
      </a>
      , autonomous home rule, union with the
      <a href="/wiki/Metropole" title="Metropole">
       metropole
      </a>
      or another state), or culturally (removal of pernicious colonial effects). The term refers particularly to the dismantlement, in the years after
      <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">
       World War II
      </a>
      , of the
      <a href="/wiki/Colonial_empire" title="Colonial empire">
       colonial empires
      </a>
      established prior to
      <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">
       World War I
      </a>
      throughout the world.
     </p>
     <p>
      The
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_Nations_Special_Committee_on_Decolonization" title="United Nations Special Committee on Decolonization">
       United Nations Special Committee on Decolonization
      </a>
      has stated that in the process of decolonization there is no alternative to the colonizer allowing a process of
      <a href="/wiki/Self-determination" title="Self-determination">
       self-determination
      </a>
      ,
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
         <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2010)">
          citation needed
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
      but in practice decolonization may involve either
      <a href="/wiki/Nonviolent_revolution" title="Nonviolent revolution">
       nonviolent revolution
      </a>
      or
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/National_liberation_wars" title="National liberation wars">
       national liberation wars
      </a>
      by pro-independence groups. It may be intramural or involve the intervention of foreign powers acting individually or through international bodies such as the
      <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">
       United Nations
      </a>
      . Although examples of decolonization can be found as early as the writings of
      <a href="/wiki/Thucydides" title="Thucydides">
       Thucydides
      </a>
      , there have been several particularly active periods of decolonization in modern times. These include the
      <a href="/wiki/Spanish_American_wars_of_independence" title="Spanish American wars of independence">
       breakup of the Spanish Empire
      </a>
      in the 19th century; of the
      <a href="/wiki/German_Empire" title="German Empire">
       German
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Austria-Hungary" title="Austria-Hungary">
       Austro-Hungarian
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">
       Ottoman
      </a>
      , and
      <a href="/wiki/Russian_Empire" title="Russian Empire">
       Russian Empires
      </a>
      following World War I; of the
      <a href="/wiki/British_Empire" title="British Empire">
       British
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/French_colonial_empire" title="French colonial empire">
       French
      </a>
      ,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dutch_colonial_empire" title="Dutch colonial empire">
       Dutch
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Japanese_colonial_empire" title="Japanese colonial empire">
       Japanese
      </a>
      ,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Portuguese_colonial_empire" title="Portuguese colonial empire">
       Portuguese
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Belgian_colonial_empire" title="Belgian colonial empire">
       Belgian
      </a>
      and
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Italian_colonial_empire" title="Italian colonial empire">
       Italian colonial empires
      </a>
      following World War II; and of the
      <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">
       Soviet Union
      </a>
      (successor to the
      <a href="/wiki/Russian_Empire" title="Russian Empire">
       Russian Empire
      </a>
      )
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2">
       <a href="#cite_note-2">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        2
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      following the
      <a href="/wiki/Cold_War" title="Cold War">
       Cold War
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <table class="mbox-small plainlinks sistersitebox" style="border:1px solid #aaa;background-color:#f9f9f9">

        </div>

     <p>
      As a philosophy, "decolonization" refers to the ability to view and discuss non-European cultures from an unbiased, non-Western perspective.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3">
       <a href="#cite_note-3">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        3
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4">
       <a href="#cite_note-4">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        4
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
     </p>

     <p>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Methods_and_stages">
       Methods and stages
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Decolonization&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Methods and stages">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <p>
      Decolonization is a political process, frequently involving violence. In extreme circumstances, there is a
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/War_of_Independence" title="War of Independence">
       war of independence
      </a>
      , sometimes following a revolution. More often, there is a dynamic cycle where negotiations fail, minor disturbances ensue resulting in suppression by the police and military forces, escalating into more violent
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Revolt" title="Revolt">
       revolts
      </a>
      that lead to further negotiations until independence is granted. In rare cases, the actions of the pro-independence movements are characterized by
      <a href="/wiki/Nonviolence" title="Nonviolence">
       nonviolence
      </a>
      , with the
      <a href="/wiki/Indian_independence_movement" title="Indian independence movement">
       Indian independence movement
      </a>
      led by
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mohandas_Karamchand_Gandhi" title="Mohandas Karamchand Gandhi">
       Mohandas Karamchand Gandhi
      </a>
      being one of the most notable examples, and the violence comes as active suppression from the occupying forces or as political opposition from forces representing minority local communities who feel threatened by the prospect of independence. For example, there was a war of independence in
      <a href="/wiki/French_Indochina" title="French Indochina">
       French Indochina
      </a>
      , while in some countries in
      <a href="/wiki/French_West_Africa" title="French West Africa">
       French West Africa
      </a>
      (excluding the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Maghreb" title="Maghreb">
       Maghreb
      </a>
      countries) decolonization resulted from a combination of insurrection and negotiation. The process is only complete when the
      <i>
       de facto
      </i>
      government of the newly independent country is recognized as the
      <i>
       de jure
      </i>
      <a href="/wiki/Sovereign_state" title="Sovereign state">
       sovereign state
      </a>
      by the community of nations.
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
         <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2015)">
          citation needed
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Independence is often difficult to achieve without the encouragement and practical support from one or more external parties. The motives for giving such aid are varied: nations of the same ethnic and/or religious stock may sympathize with the people of the country, or a strong nation may attempt to destabilize a colony as a tactical move to weaken a rival or enemy colonizing power or to create space for its own
      <a href="/wiki/Sphere_of_influence" title="Sphere of influence">
       sphere of influence
      </a>
      ; examples of this include British support of the
      <a href="/wiki/Haitian_Revolution" title="Haitian Revolution">
       Haitian Revolution
      </a>
      against France, and the
      <a href="/wiki/Monroe_Doctrine" title="Monroe Doctrine">
       Monroe Doctrine
      </a>
      of 1823, in which the United States warned the European powers not to interfere in the affairs of the newly independent states of the
      <a href="/wiki/Western_Hemisphere" title="Western Hemisphere">
       Western Hemisphere
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <p>
      As world opinion became more pro-independence following
      <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">
       World War I
      </a>
      , there was an
      <i>
       institutionalised collective effort
      </i>
      to advance the cause of decolonization through the
      <a href="/wiki/League_of_Nations" title="League of Nations">
       League of Nations
      </a>
      . Under Article 22 of the Covenant of the League of Nations, a number of
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/League_of_Nations_Mandate" title="League of Nations Mandate">
       mandates
      </a>
      were created. The expressed intention was to prepare these countries for self-government, but are often interpreted as a mere redistribution of control over the former colonies of the defeated powers, mainly Germany and the
      <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">
       Ottoman Empire
      </a>
      . This reassignment work continued through the
      <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">
       United Nations
      </a>
      , with a similar system of
      <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Trust_Territories" title="United Nations Trust Territories">
       trust territories
      </a>
      created to adjust control over both former colonies and mandated territories.
     </p>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Gungu_la_mcezo_contre_la_France_%C3%A0_Mayotte.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2165" data-file-width="3388" height="141" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Gungu_la_mcezo_contre_la_France_%C3%A0_Mayotte.jpg/220px-Gungu_la_mcezo_contre_la_France_%C3%A0_Mayotte.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Gungu_la_mcezo_contre_la_France_%C3%A0_Mayotte.jpg/330px-Gungu_la_mcezo_contre_la_France_%C3%A0_Mayotte.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Gungu_la_mcezo_contre_la_France_%C3%A0_Mayotte.jpg/440px-Gungu_la_mcezo_contre_la_France_%C3%A0_Mayotte.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Gungu_la_mcezo_contre_la_France_%C3%A0_Mayotte.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Comorans protest
        <a href="/wiki/Mahoran_status_referendum,_2009" title="Mahoran status referendum, 2009">
         Mayotte referendum
        </a>
        on becoming an overseas department of France, 2009
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      In referendums, some colonial populations have chosen to retain their colonial status, such as
      <a href="/wiki/Gibraltar" title="Gibraltar">
       Gibraltar
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/French_Guiana" title="French Guiana">
       French Guiana
      </a>
      . There are even examples, such as the
      <a href="/wiki/Falklands_War" title="Falklands War">
       Falklands War
      </a>
      , in which an Imperial power goes to war to defend the right of a colony to continue to be a colony. Colonial powers have sometimes promoted decolonization in order to shed the financial, military and other burdens that tend to grow in those colonies where the colonial governments have become more benign.
     </p>
     <p>
      Decolonization is rarely achieved through a single historical act, but rather progresses through one or more stages of decolonization, each of which can be offered or fought for: these can include the introduction of elected representatives (advisory or voting; minority or majority or even exclusive), degrees of autonomy or self-rule. Thus, the final phase of decolonisation may in fact concern little more than handing over responsibility for foreign relations and security, and soliciting
      <i>
       de jure
      </i>
      recognition for the new
      <a href="/wiki/Sovereignty" title="Sovereignty">
       sovereignty
      </a>
      . But, even following the recognition of statehood, a degree of continuity can be maintained through bilateral treaties between now equal governments involving practicalities such as military training, mutual protection pacts, or even a garrison and/or military bases.
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="History">
       History
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Decolonization&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="American_Revolution">
       American Revolution
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Decolonization&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: American Revolution">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main articles:
      <a href="/wiki/American_Revolution" title="American Revolution">
       American Revolution
      </a>
      and
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Revolutionary_War" title="Revolutionary War">
       Revolutionary War
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      Great Britain's
      <a href="/wiki/Thirteen_Colonies" title="Thirteen Colonies">
       Thirteen North American colonies
      </a>
      were the first to break from the
      <a href="/wiki/British_Empire" title="British Empire">
       British Empire
      </a>
      in 1776, and were recognized as an independent nation by the
      <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Paris_(1783)" title="Treaty of Paris (1783)">
       Treaty of Paris
      </a>
      in 1783, after Britain's defeat at the hands of American militias and the French. The United States of America was the first set of European established colonies to achieve independence and establish itself as a nation, and was the first independent nation in the Americas.
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Decolonization_of_Spanish_America">
       Decolonization of Spanish America
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Decolonization&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Decolonization of Spanish America">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/Decolonization_of_the_Americas" title="Decolonization of the Americas">
       Decolonization of the Americas
      </a>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:JuraIndependencia.jpg">
        <img alt="Portrait of the Chilean declaration of independence" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="709" data-file-width="1077" height="145" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/JuraIndependencia.jpg/220px-JuraIndependencia.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/JuraIndependencia.jpg/330px-JuraIndependencia.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/JuraIndependencia.jpg/440px-JuraIndependencia.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:JuraIndependencia.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        The
        <a href="/wiki/Chilean_Declaration_of_Independence" title="Chilean Declaration of Independence">
         Chilean Declaration of Independence
        </a>
        on 18 February 1818
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      With the invasion of Spain by Napoleon in 1806, the American colonies declared autonomy and loyalty to the King Fernand VII. The Contract was broken and the regions of the Spanish Empire had to decide whether to show allegiance to the Junta of Cadiz (the only territory in Spain free from Napoleon) or have a junta (assembly) of its own. The economic monopoly of the metropolis was the main reason why many countries decided to become independent from Spain. In 1809, the independence wars of Latin America begun with a revolt in La Paz, Bolivia. In 1807 and 1808, the Vice Royalty of the River Plate was invaded by the English, after their 2nd defeat a Frenchman called Santiague de Liniers was proclaimed new Vice Roi by the local population, and later accepted by Spain. In May 1810 in Buenos Aires, a Junta was created, but in Montevideo it was not recognized by the local government who followed the authority of the Junta of Cadiz, the rivalry between the 2 harbors was the main reason for the distrust between the 2 cities. During the next 15 years, the Spanish and Royalist on one side, and the rebels fought in South America and Mexico. Numerous countries declared their independence. In 1824, the Spanish forces were defeated in the Battle of Ayacucho. The mainland was free and in 1898, Spain lost Cuba and Puerto Rico in the SpanishAmerican War, Puerto Rico became a Colony of the U.S.A. but Cuba was independent in 1902.
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Decolonization_of_the_Ottoman_Empire">
       Decolonization of the Ottoman Empire
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Decolonization&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Decolonization of the Ottoman Empire">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main articles:
      <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Question" title="Eastern Question">
       Eastern Question
      </a>
      and
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rise_of_nationalism_under_the_Ottoman_Empire" title="Rise of nationalism under the Ottoman Empire">
       Rise of nationalism under the Ottoman Empire
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      A number of peoples (mainly
      <a href="/wiki/Christian" title="Christian">
       Christians
      </a>
      in the
      <a href="/wiki/Balkans" title="Balkans">
       Balkans
      </a>
      ) previously conquered by the
      <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">
       Ottoman Empire
      </a>
      were able to achieve independence in the 19th century, a process that peaked at the time of the Ottoman defeat in the
      <a href="/wiki/Russo-Turkish_War_(1877%E2%80%9378)" title="Russo-Turkish War (187778)">
       Russo-Turkish War
      </a>
      of 187778.
     </p>
     <p>
      The Ottoman Empire had failed to raise revenue and a monopoly of effective armed forces.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5">
       <a href="#cite_note-5">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        5
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      This may have caused the fall of the Ottoman Empire.
     </p>
     <h4>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Egypt">
       Egypt
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Decolonization&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Egypt">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h4>
     <div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/Muhammad_Ali%27s_seizure_of_power" title="Muhammad Ali's seizure of power">
       Muhammad Ali's seizure of power
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      In the wake of the 1798
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/French_Invasion_of_Egypt" title="French Invasion of Egypt">
       French Invasion of Egypt
      </a>
      and its subsequent expulsion in 1801, the commander of an
      <a href="/wiki/Albanian_Pashaliks" title="Albanian Pashaliks">
       Albanian
      </a>
      regiment,
      <a href="/wiki/Muhammad_Ali_of_Egypt" title="Muhammad Ali of Egypt">
       Muhammad Ali
      </a>
      , was able to gain control of
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Egypt_Province,_Ottoman_Empire" title="Egypt Province, Ottoman Empire">
       Egypt
      </a>
      . Although he was acknowledged by the
      <a href="/wiki/Selim_III" title="Selim III">
       Sultan
      </a>
      in
      <a href="/wiki/Istanbul" title="Istanbul">
       Constantinople
      </a>
      in 1805 as his
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Pasha" title="Pasha">
        pasha
       </a>
      </i>
      , Muhammad Ali, and eventually his successors, were facto monarchs of a largely independent state managing its own foreign relations. However, despite this de facto independence, Egypt did remain nominally a vassal state of the Ottoman Empire obliged to pay a hefty annual tribute to the Sultan. The Ottoman Empire's residual powers over Egypt remained a threat to its independence, as was shown in 1882 when Great Britain, with the Sultan's agreement, occupied Egypt permanently. Upon declaring war on Turkey in November 1914, Britain unilaterally declared the Sultan's rights and title over Egypt abolished and
      <a href="/wiki/History_of_Egypt_under_the_British" title="History of Egypt under the British">
       proclaimed its own protectorate
      </a>
      over the country.
     </p>
     <h4>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Greece">
       Greece
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Decolonization&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Greece">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h4>
     <div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/Greek_War_of_Independence" title="Greek War of Independence">
       Greek War of Independence
      </a>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Marsigli_Filippo_-_The_Death_of_Markos_Botsaris_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2540" data-file-width="3705" height="151" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/Marsigli_Filippo_-_The_Death_of_Markos_Botsaris_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg/220px-Marsigli_Filippo_-_The_Death_of_Markos_Botsaris_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/Marsigli_Filippo_-_The_Death_of_Markos_Botsaris_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg/330px-Marsigli_Filippo_-_The_Death_of_Markos_Botsaris_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/Marsigli_Filippo_-_The_Death_of_Markos_Botsaris_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg/440px-Marsigli_Filippo_-_The_Death_of_Markos_Botsaris_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Marsigli_Filippo_-_The_Death_of_Markos_Botsaris_-_Google_Art_Project.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Greek War of Independence
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      The Greek War of Independence (18211829) was fought to liberate Greece from a three centuries long
      <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">
       Ottoman
      </a>
      occupation. Independence was secured by the intervention of the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/British_Navy" title="British Navy">
       British
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/French_Navy" title="French Navy">
       French navies
      </a>
      and the
      <a href="/wiki/French_Army" title="French Army">
       French
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Imperial_Russian_Army" title="Imperial Russian Army">
       Russian armies
      </a>
      , but Greece was limited to an area including perhaps only one-third of ethnic Greeks, that later grew significantly with the
      <a href="/wiki/Megali_Idea" title="Megali Idea">
       Megali Idea
      </a>
      project. The war ended many of the privileges of the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Phanariot" title="Phanariot">
       Phanariot
      </a>
      Greeks of
      <a href="/wiki/Istanbul" title="Istanbul">
       Constantinople
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <h4>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Bulgaria">
       Bulgaria
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Decolonization&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Bulgaria">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h4>
     <div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/Bulgarian_National_Revival" title="Bulgarian National Revival">
       Bulgarian National Revival
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      Following a
      <a href="/wiki/April_Uprising" title="April Uprising">
       failed Bulgarian revolt
      </a>
      in 1876, the subsequent
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Russo-Turkish_War,_1877-1878" title="Russo-Turkish War, 1877-1878">
       Russo-Turkish war
      </a>
      ended with the provisional
      <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_San_Stefano" title="Treaty of San Stefano">
       Treaty of San Stefano
      </a>
      established a huge new realm of Bulgaria including most of
      <a href="/wiki/Macedonia_(region)" title="Macedonia (region)">
       Macedonia
      </a>
      and
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Thrace_(region)" title="Thrace (region)">
       Thrace
      </a>
      . The final
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Berlin,_1878" title="Treaty of Berlin, 1878">
       1878 Treaty of Berlin
      </a>
      allowed the other Great Powers to limit the size of the new Russian
      <a href="/wiki/Client_state" title="Client state">
       client state
      </a>
      and even briefly divided this rump state in two, Bulgaria and
      <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Rumelia" title="Eastern Rumelia">
       Eastern Rumelia
      </a>
      , but the
      <a href="/wiki/Irredentism" title="Irredentism">
       irredentist
      </a>
      claims from the first treaty would direct Bulgarian claims through the
      <a href="/wiki/First_Balkan_War" title="First Balkan War">
       first
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Second_Balkan_War" title="Second Balkan War">
       second Balkan Wars
      </a>
      and both World Wars.
     </p>
     <h4>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Romania">
       Romania
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Decolonization&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Romania">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h4>
     <div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/National_awakening_of_Romania" title="National awakening of Romania">
       National awakening of Romania
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      Romania fought on the Russian side in the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Russo-Turkish_War,_1877-78" title="Russo-Turkish War, 1877-78">
       Russo-Turkish War
      </a>
      and in the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Berlin,_1878" title="Treaty of Berlin, 1878">
       1878 Treaty of Berlin
      </a>
      , Romania was recognized as an
      <a href="/wiki/Romanian_War_of_Independence" title="Romanian War of Independence">
       independent
      </a>
      state by the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Great_Powers" title="Great Powers">
       Great Powers
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6">
       <a href="#cite_note-6">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        6
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7">
       <a href="#cite_note-7">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        7
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8">
       <a href="#cite_note-8">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        8
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Boyd_9-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-Boyd-9">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        9
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h4>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Serbia">
       Serbia
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Decolonization&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Serbia">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h4>
     <div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article:
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Serbian_revolution" title="Serbian revolution">
       Serbian revolution
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      Centuries
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sdc_10-0">
       <a href="#cite_note-sdc-10">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        10
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      of armed and unarmed struggle ended with the recognition of
      <a href="/wiki/Serbia" title="Serbia">
       Serbian
      </a>
      independence from the Ottoman Empire at the
      <a href="/wiki/Congress_of_Berlin" title="Congress of Berlin">
       Congress of Berlin
      </a>
      in 1878.
     </p>
     <h4>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Montenegro">
       Montenegro
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Decolonization&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Montenegro">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h4>
     <p>
      The independence of the
      <a href="/wiki/Principality_of_Montenegro" title="Principality of Montenegro">
       Principality of Montenegro
      </a>
      from the Ottoman Empire was recognized at the
      <a href="/wiki/Congress_of_Berlin" title="Congress of Berlin">
       congress of Berlin
      </a>
      in 1878. However, the Montenegrin nation has been de facto independent since 1711 (officially accepted by the
      <a href="/wiki/Tsardom_of_Russia" title="Tsardom of Russia">
       Tsardom of Russia
      </a>
      by the order of
      <a href="/wiki/Peter_the_Great" title="Peter the Great">
       Tsar Petr I Alexeyevich-Romanov
      </a>
      . In the period 1795-8, Montenegro once again claimed independence after the
      <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Krusi" title="Battle of Krusi">
       Battle of Krusi
      </a>
      . In 1806, it was recognized as a power fighting against Napoleon, meaning that it had a fully mobilized and supplied army ( by Russia, trough Admiral
      <a href="/wiki/Dmitry_Senyavin" title="Dmitry Senyavin">
       Dmitry Senyavin
      </a>
      at the Bay of
      <a href="/wiki/Kotor" title="Kotor">
       Kotor
      </a>
      ). In the period of reign of
      <a href="/wiki/Petar_II_Petrovi%C4%87-Njego%C5%A1" title="Petar II Petrovi-Njego">
       Petar II Petrovi-Njego
      </a>
      , Montenegro was again colonized by Turkey, but that changed with the coming of
      <a href="/wiki/Knyaz" title="Knyaz">
       Knyaz
      </a>
      <a href="/wiki/Danilo_I,_Prince_of_Montenegro" title="Danilo I, Prince of Montenegro">
       Danilo I
      </a>
      , with a totally successful war against Turkey in the late 1850s ending with a decisive victory of the Montenegrin army under
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Grand_Duke" title="Grand Duke">
       Grand Duke
      </a>
      <a href="/wiki/Mirko_Petrovi%C4%87-Njego%C5%A1" title="Mirko Petrovi-Njego">
       Mirko Petrovi-Njego
      </a>
      , brother of Danilo I, at the
      <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Grahovac" title="Battle of Grahovac">
       Battle of Grahovac
      </a>
      . The full independence was given to Montenegro, after almost 170 years of fighting the Turks, Bosniaks, Albanians and the French (1806-1814) at the
      <a href="/wiki/Congress_of_Berlin" title="Congress of Berlin">
       Congress of Berlin
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Decolonization_after_1918">
       Decolonization after 1918
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Decolonization&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Decolonization after 1918">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <h4>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Western_European_colonial_powers">
       Western European colonial powers
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Decolonization&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Western European colonial powers">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h4>
     <div class="hatnote">
      Further information:
      <a href="/wiki/New_Imperialism" title="New Imperialism">
       New Imperialism
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Colonialism" title="Colonialism">
       Colonialism
      </a>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Socialism_liberation.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="565" data-file-width="775" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/2/20/Socialism_liberation.jpg/200px-Socialism_liberation.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/2/20/Socialism_liberation.jpg/300px-Socialism_liberation.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/2/20/Socialism_liberation.jpg/400px-Socialism_liberation.jpg 2x" width="200"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Socialism_liberation.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Czechoslovak anti-colonialist propaganda poster: "Socialism opened the door of liberation for colonial nations."
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      The New Imperialism period, with the
      <a href="/wiki/Scramble_for_Africa" title="Scramble for Africa">
       scramble for Africa
      </a>
      and the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Opium_War" title="Opium War">
       Opium Wars
      </a>
      , marked the zenith of European colonization. It also marked the acceleration of the trends that would end it. The extraordinary material demands of the conflict had spread economic change across the world (notably inflation), and the associated social pressures of "war imperialism" created both peasant unrest and a burgeoning middle class.
     </p>
     <p>
      <a href="/wiki/Economic_growth" title="Economic growth">
       Economic growth
      </a>
      created stakeholders with their own demands, while
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Race_(classification_of_human_beings)" title="Race (classification of human beings)">
       racial
      </a>
      issues meant these people clearly stood apart from the colonial middle-class and had to form their own group. The start of mass
      <a href="/wiki/Nationalism" title="Nationalism">
       nationalism
      </a>
      , as a concept and practice, would fatally undermine the ideologies of imperialism.
     </p>
     <p>
      There were, naturally, other factors, from agrarian change (and disaster 
      <a href="/wiki/French_Indochina" title="French Indochina">
       French Indochina
      </a>
      ), changes or developments in religion (
      <a href="/wiki/Buddhism" title="Buddhism">
       Buddhism
      </a>
      in Burma,
      <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">
       Islam
      </a>
      in the
      <a href="/wiki/Dutch_East_Indies" title="Dutch East Indies">
       Dutch East Indies
      </a>
      , marginally people like
      <a href="/wiki/John_Chilembwe" title="John Chilembwe">
       John Chilembwe
      </a>
      in
      <a href="/wiki/Malawi" title="Malawi">
       Nyasaland
      </a>
      ), and the impact of the 1930s Great Depression.
     </p>
     <p>
      The
      <a href="/wiki/Great_Depression" title="Great Depression">
       Great Depression
      </a>
      , despite the concentration of its impact on the industrialized world, was also exceptionally damaging in the rural colonies. Agricultural prices fell much harder and faster than those of industrial goods. From around 1925 until
      <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">
       World War II
      </a>
      , the colonies suffered. The colonial powers concentrated on domestic issues,
      <a href="/wiki/Protectionism" title="Protectionism">
       protectionism
      </a>
      and tariffs, disregarding the damage done to international trade flows. The colonies, almost all primary "
      <a href="/wiki/Cash_crop" title="Cash crop">
       cash crop
      </a>
      " producers, lost the majority of their export income and were forced away from the "open" complementary colonial economies to "closed" systems. While some areas returned to
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Subsistence_farming" title="Subsistence farming">
       subsistence farming
      </a>
      (
      <a href="/wiki/British_Malaya" title="British Malaya">
       British Malaya
      </a>
      ) others diversified (India,
      <a href="/wiki/West_Africa" title="West Africa">
       West Africa
      </a>
      ), and some began to industrialise. These economies would not fit the colonial straitjacket when efforts were made to renew the links. Further, the European-owned and -run
      <a href="/wiki/Plantation" title="Plantation">
       plantations
      </a>
      proved more vulnerable to extended
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Deflation_(economics)" title="Deflation (economics)">
       deflation
      </a>
      than native
      <a href="/wiki/Capitalism" title="Capitalism">
       capitalists
      </a>
      , reducing the dominance of "white" farmers in colonial economies and making the European
      <a href="/wiki/Government" title="Government">
       governments
      </a>
      and investors of the 1930s co-opt
      <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_peoples" title="Indigenous peoples">
       indigenous
      </a>
      elites  despite the implications for the future. Colonial reform also hastened their end; notably the move from non-interventionist collaborative systems towards directed, disruptive, direct management to drive economic change. The creation of genuine bureaucratic government boosted the formation of indigenous
      <a href="/wiki/Bourgeoisie" title="Bourgeoisie">
       bourgeoisie
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <h4>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="United_Kingdom">
       United Kingdom
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Decolonization&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: United Kingdom">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h4>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:192px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Easter_1916.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1909" data-file-width="1273" height="285" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Easter_1916.jpg/190px-Easter_1916.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Easter_1916.jpg/285px-Easter_1916.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Easter_1916.jpg/380px-Easter_1916.jpg 2x" width="190"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Easter_1916.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        A mural in
        <a href="/wiki/Belfast" title="Belfast">
         Belfast
        </a>
        depicting the
        <a href="/wiki/Easter_Rising" title="Easter Rising">
         Easter Rising
        </a>
        of 1916
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      The emergence of indigenous bourgeois elites was especially characteristic of the
      <a href="/wiki/British_Empire" title="British Empire">
       British Empire
      </a>
      , which seemed less capable (or less ruthless) in controlling political nationalism. Driven by pragmatic demands of budgets and manpower the British made deals with the nationalist elites. Across the empire, the general protocol was to convene a constitutional conference in London to discuss the transition to greater self-government and then independence, submit a report of the constitutional conference to parliament, if approved submit a bill to Parliament at Westminster to terminate the responsibility of the United Kingdom (with a copy of the new constitution annexed), and finally, if approved, issuance of an Order of Council fixing the exact date of independence.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11">
       <a href="#cite_note-11">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        11
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      London dealt with the white
      <a href="/wiki/Dominion" title="Dominion">
       dominions
      </a>
      , retained strategic resources at the cost of reducing direct control in Egypt, and made numerous reforms in the
      <a href="/wiki/British_Raj" title="British Raj">
       British Raj
      </a>
      , culminating in the
      <a href="/wiki/Government_of_India_Act_1935" title="Government of India Act 1935">
       Government of India Act
      </a>
      (1935). Despite these efforts though, the British Government continued to slowly lose their control of the Raj. The end of World War II allowed India, in addition to various other European colonies, to take advantage of the postwar chaos that had begun to exist in Europe during the mid-1940s.
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mohandas_Karamchand_Gandhi" title="Mohandas Karamchand Gandhi">
       Mohandas Karamchand Gandhi
      </a>
      , India's independence movement leader, realized the advantage in conducting a peaceful resistance to the British Empire's attempts to retake control of their "crown jewel". By becoming a symbol of both peace and opposition to British imperialism, many Indian citizens began to view the British as the cause of India's problems leading to a newfound sense of
      <a href="/wiki/Nationalist_Movements_in_India" title="Nationalist Movements in India">
       nationalism
      </a>
      among its population. With this new wave of Indian nationalism, Gandhi was eventually able to garner the support needed to push back the British and create an independent India in 1947.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12">
       <a href="#cite_note-12">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        12
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Tropical Africa was only fully drawn into the colonial system at the end of the 19th century. In the north-east the continued independence of the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Empire_of_Ethiopia" title="Empire of Ethiopia">
       Empire of Ethiopia
      </a>
      remained a beacon of hope to pro-independence activists. However, with the anti-colonial wars of the 1900s (decade) barely over, new modernising forms of African Nationalism began to gain strength in the early 20th-century with the emergence of Pan-Africanism, as advocated by the Jamaican journalist
      <a href="/wiki/Marcus_Garvey" title="Marcus Garvey">
       Marcus Garvey
      </a>
      (18871940) whose widely distributed newspapers demanded swift abolition of European imperialism, as well as republicanism in Egypt.
      <a href="/wiki/Kwame_Nkrumah" title="Kwame Nkrumah">
       Kwame Nkrumah
      </a>
      (19091972) who was inspired by the works of Garvey led Ghana to independence from colonial rule.
     </p>
     <table class="metadata plainlinks ambox ambox-style ambox-Cleanup" role="presentation">
      <tr>
       <td class="mbox-image">

        </div>
       </td>
       <td class="mbox-text">
        <span class="mbox-text-span">

          <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Cleanup" title="Wikipedia:Cleanup">

          </a>
          to meet Wikipedia's

           quality standards
          </a>
         </b>
         .
         <span class="hide-when-compact">
          No
          <a href="/wiki/Template:Cleanup/doc" title="Template:Cleanup/doc">
