     <h4>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="United_States">
       United States
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Decolonization&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: United States">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h4>
     <table class="metadata plainlinks ambox ambox-content ambox-POV" role="presentation">
      <tr>
       <td class="mbox-image">
        <div style="width:52px">
         <img alt="Unbalanced scales.svg" data-file-height="354" data-file-width="400" height="40" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Unbalanced_scales.svg/45px-Unbalanced_scales.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Unbalanced_scales.svg/68px-Unbalanced_scales.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Unbalanced_scales.svg/90px-Unbalanced_scales.svg.png 2x" width="45"/>
        </div>
       </td>
       <td class="mbox-text">
        <span class="mbox-text-span">
         The
         <b>
          <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Neutral_point_of_view" title="Wikipedia:Neutral point of view">
           neutrality
          </a>
          of this article is
          <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:NPOV_dispute" title="Wikipedia:NPOV dispute">
           disputed
          </a>
         </b>
         .
         <span class="hide-when-compact">
          Relevant discussion may be found on the
          <a href="/wiki/Talk:Decolonization#.23" title="Talk:Decolonization">
           talk page
          </a>
          . Please do not remove this message until the
          <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:NPOV_dispute#What_is_an_NPOV_dispute.3F" title="Wikipedia:NPOV dispute">
           dispute is resolved
          </a>
          .
         </span>
         <small>
          <i>
           (December 2010)
          </i>
         </small>
        </span>
       </td>
      </tr>
     </table>
     <div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main articles:
      <a href="/wiki/American_imperialism" title="American imperialism">
       American imperialism
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Timeline_of_United_States_military_operations" title="Timeline of United States military operations">
       Timeline of United States military operations
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      A former colony itself, the United States approached imperialism differently from the Great Powers and Japan. Much of its energy and rapidly expanding population was directed westward across the North American continent against
      <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_peoples_of_the_Americas" title="Indigenous peoples of the Americas">
       American Indians
      </a>
      , France, English territorial pretensions,
      <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Empire" title="Spanish Empire">
       Spain
      </a>
      , and Mexico. With eventual assistance from the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/British_Navy" title="British Navy">
       British Navy
      </a>
      , its
      <a href="/wiki/Monroe_Doctrine" title="Monroe Doctrine">
       Monroe Doctrine
      </a>
      reserved the Americas as its sphere of interest, prohibiting other states (particularly Spain) from recolonizing the recently freed polities of
      <a href="/wiki/Latin_America" title="Latin America">
       Latin America
      </a>
      and other states like France and the UK from acquiring new colonies in the mainland, yet the French were allowed to support the Mexican monarchy and the Spaniards fought several wars against Chile and Peru for the guano deposits of their islands. Economic and political pressure, as well as assaults by
      <a href="/wiki/Filibuster_(military)" title="Filibuster (military)">
       filibusters
      </a>
      , were brought to bear, but Northern fears of the expansion of slavery into new territories and the still strong Spanish Empire restrained the United States from early expansion into Cuba or
      <a href="/wiki/Central_America" title="Central America">
       Central America
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
         <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2010)">
          citation needed
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
      America's only African colony,
      <a href="/wiki/Liberia" title="Liberia">
       Liberia
      </a>
      , was formed privately and achieved independence early. While the United States had few qualms about opening the markets of
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Battles_for_Shimonoseki" title="Battles for Shimonoseki">
       Japan
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/United_States_expedition_to_Korea" title="United States expedition to Korea">
       Korea
      </a>
      , and
      <a href="/wiki/China_Relief_Expedition" title="China Relief Expedition">
       China
      </a>
      by military force, it advocated an
      <a href="/wiki/Open_Door_Policy" title="Open Door Policy">
       Open Door Policy
      </a>
      and opposed the direct division and colonization of those states even though Europeans kept doing it.
     </p>
     <p>
      Following the
      <a href="/wiki/American_Civil_War" title="American Civil War">
       Civil War
      </a>
      and particularly during and after the presidency of
      <a href="/wiki/Theodore_Roosevelt" title="Theodore Roosevelt">
       Theodore Roosevelt
      </a>
      , direct intervention in Latin America and elsewhere expanded. The United States purchased
      <a href="/wiki/Russian_America" title="Russian America">
       Russian America
      </a>
      from the tsar and accepted the offer of
      <a href="/wiki/Territory_of_Hawaii" title="Territory of Hawaii">
       Hawaii
      </a>
      from rebel expatriates and seized several colonies from Spain in 1898. Barred from annexing Cuba outright by the
      <a href="/wiki/Teller_Amendment" title="Teller Amendment">
       Teller Amendment
      </a>
      , the U.S. established it as a
      <a href="/wiki/Client_state" title="Client state">
       client state
      </a>
      with obligations including the perpetual lease of
      <a href="/wiki/Guant%C3%A1namo_Bay" title="Guantnamo Bay">
       Guantnamo Bay
      </a>
      to the U.S. Navy. The attempt of the first governor to void the island's constitution and remain in power past the end of his term provoked a rebellion that provoked a reoccupation between 1906 and 1909, but this was again followed by devolution. Similarly, the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/McKinley_administration" title="McKinley administration">
       McKinley administration
      </a>
      , despite prosecuting the
      <a href="/wiki/Philippine%E2%80%93American_War" title="PhilippineAmerican War">
       PhilippineAmerican War
      </a>
      against a
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/First_Republic_of_the_Philippines" title="First Republic of the Philippines">
       native republic
      </a>
      , set out that the
      <a href="/wiki/Territories_of_the_United_States#Former_unincorporated_territories_of_the_United_States_.28incomplete.29" title="Territories of the United States">
       Territory of the Philippine Islands
      </a>
      was eventually granted independence.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13">
       <a href="#cite_note-13">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        13
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      Britain's 1895 attempt to reject the Monroe Doctrine during the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Venezuela_Crisis_of_1895" title="Venezuela Crisis of 1895">
       Venezuela Crisis of 1895
      </a>
      , the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Venezuela_Crisis_of_1902%E2%80%931903" title="Venezuela Crisis of 19021903">
       Venezuela Crisis of 19021903
      </a>
      , and the establishment of the client state of
      <a href="/wiki/Panama" title="Panama">
       Panama
      </a>
      in 1903 via
      <a href="/wiki/Gunboat_diplomacy" title="Gunboat diplomacy">
       gunboat diplomacy
      </a>
      , however, all necessitated the maintenance of
      <a href="/wiki/Puerto_Rico" title="Puerto Rico">
       Puerto Rico
      </a>
      as a naval base to secure shipping lanes to the Caribbean and the new
      <a href="/wiki/Panama_Canal_Zone" title="Panama Canal Zone">
       canal zone
      </a>
      . In 1917, "Puerto Ricans were collectively made U.S. citizens"
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14">
       <a href="#cite_note-14">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        14
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      via the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jones-Shafroth_Act" title="Jones-Shafroth Act">
       Jones Act
      </a>
      , and in 1952 the US Congress turned the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Territory_of_Puerto_Rico" title="Territory of Puerto Rico">
       territory
      </a>
      into a
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Puerto_Rico" title="Commonwealth of Puerto Rico">
       commonwealth
      </a>
      after ratifying the
      <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Puerto_Rico" title="Constitution of Puerto Rico">
       Constitution
      </a>
      born out of United States Public Law 600.
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15">
       <a href="#cite_note-15">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        15
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      The US government then declared the territory was no longer a colony and stopped transmitting information about Puerto Rico to the United Nations Decolonization Committee. As a result, the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UN_General_Assembly_Resolution_748" title="UN General Assembly Resolution 748">
       UN General Assembly
      </a>
      removed Puerto Rico from the
      <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_list_of_Non-Self-Governing_Territories" title="United Nations list of Non-Self-Governing Territories">
       U.N. list of non-self-governing territories
      </a>
      . Dissatisfied with their new political status, Puerto Ricans turned to political referendums to let make their opinions known. Several internal plebiscites, non-binding upon the United States, proposing
      <a href="/wiki/U.S._state" title="U.S. state">
       statehood
      </a>
      or independence for the island did not garnish a majority in 1967, 1993, and 1998. As a result of the UN not applying the full set of criteria which was enunciated in 1960 when it took favorable note of the cessation of transmission of information regarding the non-self-governing status of Puerto Rico,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16">
       <a href="#cite_note-16">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        16
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17">
       <a href="#cite_note-17">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        17
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      the nature of Puerto Rico's relationship with the U.S. continues to be the subject of ongoing debate in Puerto Rican politics, the
      <a href="/wiki/United_States_Congress" title="United States Congress">
       United States Congress
      </a>
      ,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18">
       <a href="#cite_note-18">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        18
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      and the
      <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">
       United Nations
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sdc_10-1">
       <a href="#cite_note-sdc-10">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        10
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19">
       <a href="#cite_note-19">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        19
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
     </p>
     <p>
      The Monroe Doctrine received the
      <a href="/wiki/Roosevelt_Corollary" title="Roosevelt Corollary">
       Roosevelt Corollary
      </a>
      in 1904, providing that the United States had a right and obligation to intervene "in flagrant cases of such wrongdoing or impotence" that a nation in the Western Hemisphere became vulnerable to European control. In practice, this meant that the United States was led to act as a collections agent for European creditors by administering customs duties in the
      <a href="/wiki/Dominican_Republic" title="Dominican Republic">
       Dominican Republic
      </a>
      (19051941),
      <a href="/wiki/Haiti" title="Haiti">
       Haiti
      </a>
      (19151934), and elsewhere. The intrusiveness and bad relations this engendered were somewhat checked by the
      <a href="/wiki/Clark_Memorandum" title="Clark Memorandum">
       Clark Memorandum
      </a>
      and renounced by President
      <a href="/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt" title="Franklin D. Roosevelt">
       Franklin D. Roosevelt
      </a>
      's "
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Good_Neighbor_Policy" title="Good Neighbor Policy">
       Good Neighbor Policy
      </a>
      ." The end of World War II saw America producing 46% of the world's GDP,
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20">
       <a href="#cite_note-20">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        20
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      but pouring billions of dollars into the
      <a href="/wiki/Marshall_Plan" title="Marshall Plan">
       Marshall Plan
      </a>
      and restoring independent (if anti-Communist) democracies in Japan and
      <a href="/wiki/West_Germany" title="West Germany">
       West Germany
      </a>
      . The post-war period also saw America push hard to accelerate decolonialization and bring an end to the colonial empires of its Western allies, most importantly during the 1956
      <a href="/wiki/Suez_Crisis" title="Suez Crisis">
       Suez Crisis
      </a>
      , but American military bases were established around the world and direct and indirect interventions continued in
      <a href="/wiki/Korean_War" title="Korean War">
       Korea
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Vietnam_War" title="Vietnam War">
       Indochina
      </a>
      , Latin America (
      <i>
       inter alia
      </i>
      , the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1965_United_States_occupation_of_the_Dominican_Republic" title="1965 United States occupation of the Dominican Republic">
       1965 occupation of the Dominican Republic
      </a>
      ), Africa, and the Middle East to oppose Communist invasions and insurgencies. Since the dissolution of the Soviet Union, the United States has been far less active in the Americas, but invaded
      <a href="/wiki/War_in_Afghanistan_(2001%E2%80%93present)" title="War in Afghanistan (2001present)">
       Afghanistan
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Iraq_War" title="Iraq War">
       Iraq
      </a>
      following the
      <a href="/wiki/September_11_attacks" title="September 11 attacks">
       September 11 attacks
      </a>
      in 2001, establishing army and air bases in
      <a href="/wiki/Central_Asia" title="Central Asia">
       Central Asia
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <h4>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Japan">
       Japan
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Decolonization&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Japan">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h4>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:US_Army_in_Korea_under_Japanese_Rule.JPG">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="378" data-file-width="513" height="162" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/US_Army_in_Korea_under_Japanese_Rule.JPG/220px-US_Army_in_Korea_under_Japanese_Rule.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/US_Army_in_Korea_under_Japanese_Rule.JPG/330px-US_Army_in_Korea_under_Japanese_Rule.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/US_Army_in_Korea_under_Japanese_Rule.JPG/440px-US_Army_in_Korea_under_Japanese_Rule.JPG 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:US_Army_in_Korea_under_Japanese_Rule.JPG" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        U.S. troops in
        <a href="/wiki/Korea_under_Japanese_rule" title="Korea under Japanese rule">
         Korea
        </a>
        , September 1945
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      Japan had gained several substantial colonial possessions in East Asia such as Taiwan and Korea. Pursuing a colonial policy comparable to those of European powers, Japan settled significant populations of ethnic Japanese in its colonies while simultaneously suppressing indigenous ethnic populations by enforcing the learning and use of the
      <a href="/wiki/Japanese_language" title="Japanese language">
       Japanese language
      </a>
      in schools. Other methods such as public interaction, and attempts to eradicate the use of
      <a href="/wiki/Korean_language" title="Korean language">
       Korean
      </a>
      ,
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hokkien_dialect" title="Hokkien dialect">
       Hokkien
      </a>
      , and
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hakka_(language)" title="Hakka (language)">
       Hakka
      </a>
      among the indigenous peoples, were seen to be used. Japan also set up
      <a href="/wiki/National_Seven_Universities" title="National Seven Universities">
       Imperial universities
      </a>
      in Korea (
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Keijo_Imperial_University" title="Keijo Imperial University">
       Keijo Imperial University
      </a>
      ) and Taiwan (
      <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Taihoku_University&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Taihoku University (page does not exist)">
       Taihoku University
      </a>
      ) to compel education.
     </p>
     <p>
      World War II gave the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Japanese_Empire" title="Japanese Empire">
       Japanese Empire
      </a>
      occasion to conquer vast swaths of Asia, sweeping into China and seizing the Western colonies of Vietnam,
      <a href="/wiki/Hong_Kong" title="Hong Kong">
       Hong Kong
      </a>
      , the Philippines, Burma,
      <a href="/wiki/British_Malaya" title="British Malaya">
       Malaya
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Timor" title="Portuguese Timor">
       Timor
      </a>
      and Indonesia among others, albeit only for the duration of the war. An estimated 20 million Chinese died during the
      <a href="/wiki/Second_Sino-Japanese_War" title="Second Sino-Japanese War">
       Second Sino-Japanese War
      </a>
      (19311945).
      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21">
       <a href="#cite_note-21">
        <span>
         [
        </span>
        21
        <span>
         ]
        </span>
       </a>
      </sup>
      Following its surrender to the
      <a href="/wiki/Allies_of_World_War_II" title="Allies of World War II">
       Allies
      </a>
      in 1945, Japan was deprived of all its colonies. Japan further claims that the southern
      <a href="/wiki/Kuril_Islands" title="Kuril Islands">
       Kuril Islands
      </a>
      are a small portion of its own national territory, occupied by the
      <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">
       Soviet Union
      </a>
      soon after
      <a href="/wiki/Soviet%E2%80%93Japanese_War_(1945)" title="SovietJapanese War (1945)">
       it declared war on Japan in August 1945
      </a>
      , and later annexed.
     </p>
     <h4>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="French_decolonization">
       French decolonization
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Decolonization&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: French decolonization">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h4>
     <div class="hatnote">
      Further information:
      <a href="/wiki/French_colonial_empire" title="French colonial empire">
       French colonial empire
      </a>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Manifestation_nationalistes_du_8_mai_1945_S%C3%A9tif.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="443" data-file-width="590" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Manifestation_nationalistes_du_8_mai_1945_S%C3%A9tif.jpg/220px-Manifestation_nationalistes_du_8_mai_1945_S%C3%A9tif.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Manifestation_nationalistes_du_8_mai_1945_S%C3%A9tif.jpg/330px-Manifestation_nationalistes_du_8_mai_1945_S%C3%A9tif.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/Manifestation_nationalistes_du_8_mai_1945_S%C3%A9tif.jpg/440px-Manifestation_nationalistes_du_8_mai_1945_S%C3%A9tif.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Manifestation_nationalistes_du_8_mai_1945_S%C3%A9tif.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Anti-French protests in Algeria on 8 May 1945
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      After World War I, the colonized people were frustrated at France's failure to recognize the effort provided by the French colonies (resources, but more importantly colonial troops - the famous
      <i>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tirailleurs" title="Tirailleurs">
        tirailleurs
       </a>
      </i>
      ). Although in
      <a href="/wiki/Paris" title="Paris">
       Paris
      </a>
      the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Great_Mosque_of_Paris" title="Great Mosque of Paris">
       Great Mosque of Paris
      </a>
      was constructed as recognition of these efforts, the French state had no intention to allow
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Self-rule" title="Self-rule">
       self-rule
      </a>
      , let alone grant
      <a href="/wiki/Independence" title="Independence">
       independence
      </a>
      to the colonized people. Thus,
      <a href="/wiki/Nationalism" title="Nationalism">
       nationalism
      </a>
      in the colonies became stronger in between the two wars, leading to
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Muhammad_Ibn_%27Abd_al-Karim_al-Khattabi" title="Muhammad Ibn 'Abd al-Karim al-Khattabi">
       Abd el-Krim
      </a>
      's
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rif_War_(1920)" title="Rif War (1920)">
       Rif War
      </a>
      (19211925) in
      <a href="/wiki/History_of_Morocco" title="History of Morocco">
       Morocco
      </a>
      and to the creation of
      <a href="/wiki/Messali_Hadj" title="Messali Hadj">
       Messali Hadj
      </a>
      's
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Star_of_North_Africa" title="Star of North Africa">
       Star of North Africa
      </a>
      in
      <a href="/wiki/Nationalism_and_resistance_in_Algeria" title="Nationalism and resistance in Algeria">
       Algeria
      </a>
      in 1925. However, these movements would gain full potential only after World War II. The October 27, 1946 Constitution creating the
      <a href="/wiki/French_Fourth_Republic" title="French Fourth Republic">
       Fourth Republic
      </a>
      substituted the
      <a href="/wiki/French_Union" title="French Union">
       French Union
      </a>
      to the colonial empire. On the night of March 29, 1947, a
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Madagascar_revolt" title="Madagascar revolt">
       nationalist uprising in Madagascar
      </a>
      led the French government headed by
      <a href="/wiki/Paul_Ramadier" title="Paul Ramadier">
       Paul Ramadier
      </a>
      (
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Section_Fran%C3%A7aise_de_l%27Internationale_Ouvri%C3%A8re" title="Section Franaise de l'Internationale Ouvrire">
       Socialist
      </a>
      ) to violent repression: one year of bitter fighting, 11,000-40,000 Malagasy died. On May 8, 1945, the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/S%C3%A9tif_massacre" title="Stif massacre">
       Stif massacre
      </a>
      took place in Algeria.
     </p>
     <p>
      In 1946, the states of
      <a href="/wiki/French_Indochina" title="French Indochina">
       French Indochina
      </a>
      withdrew from the Union, leading to the
      <a href="/wiki/First_Indochina_War" title="First Indochina War">
       Indochina War
      </a>
      (194654) against
      <a href="/wiki/Ho_Chi_Minh" title="Ho Chi Minh">
       Ho Chi Minh
      </a>
      , who had been a co-founder of the
      <a href="/wiki/French_Communist_Party" title="French Communist Party">
       French Communist Party
      </a>
      in 1920 and had founded the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vietminh" title="Vietminh">
       Vietminh
      </a>
      in 1941. In 1956, Morocco and
      <a href="/wiki/History_of_Tunisia" title="History of Tunisia">
       Tunisia
      </a>
      gained their independence, while the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Algerian_War_of_Independence" title="Algerian War of Independence">
       Algerian War
      </a>
      was raging (19541962). Similarly, a decade earlier,
      <a href="/wiki/Laos" title="Laos">
       Laos
      </a>
      and
      <a href="/wiki/Cambodia" title="Cambodia">
       Cambodia
      </a>
      achieved independence in order for the French to focus to keeping Vietnam. With
      <a href="/wiki/Charles_de_Gaulle" title="Charles de Gaulle">
       Charles de Gaulle
      </a>
      's return to power in 1958 amidst turmoil and threats of a right-wing coups d'tat to protect "French Algeria", the decolonization was completed with the independence of Sub-Saharan Africa's colonies in 1960 and the March 19, 1962
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Evian_Accords" title="Evian Accords">
       Evian Accords
      </a>
      , which put an end to the Algerian war. The
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Organisation_arm%C3%A9e_secr%C3%A8te" title="Organisation arme secrte">
       OAS
      </a>
      movement unsuccessfully tried to block the accords with a series of bombings, including an attempted assassination against Charles de Gaulle.
     </p>
     <p>
      To this day, the Algerian war  officially called until the 1990s a "public order operation"  remains a trauma for both France and Algeria. Philosopher
      <a href="/wiki/Paul_Ric%C5%93ur" title="Paul Ricur">
       Paul Ricur
      </a>
      has spoken of the necessity of a "decolonization of memory", starting with the recognition of the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1961_Paris_massacre" title="1961 Paris massacre">
       1961 Paris massacre
      </a>
      during the Algerian war and the recognition of the decisive role of African and especially North African immigrant manpower in the
      <i>
       <a href="/wiki/Trente_Glorieuses" title="Trente Glorieuses">
        Trente Glorieuses
       </a>
      </i>
      postWorld War II economic growth period. In the 1960s, due to economic needs for post-war reconstruction and rapid economic growth, French employers actively sought to recruit manpower from the colonies, explaining today's
      <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_France" title="Demographics of France">
       multiethnic population
      </a>
      .
     </p>
     <h4>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="The_Soviet_Union">
       The Soviet Union
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Decolonization&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: The Soviet Union">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h4>
     <p>
      The Soviet Union, following the conclusion of the
      <a href="/wiki/Russian_Civil_War" title="Russian Civil War">
       Russian Civil War
      </a>
      in 1922, continued the Tsar's colonial policies in most of the former Russian Empire and its vassals such as Mongolia. Initially, the nations of Finland, Poland, Estonia, Latvia, and Lithuania were recognized as independent nations, but Soviet policy shifted towards colonialism during the rise of Joseph Stalin. The policy shift was additionally boosted by the rise of Nazi Germany in the 1930s. Of the nations that comprised former Russian Empire, only Finland would remain independent throughout the Cold War. Soviet colonial policy was most famously marked by the use of violent repression against civil disobedience in Prague in 1968 (see
      <a href="/wiki/Prague_Spring" title="Prague Spring">
       Prague Spring
      </a>
      ) and in Hungary in 1956.
     </p>
     <p>
      The era of Soviet colonialism would ultimately end due to numerous anti-colonialism efforts of individuals such as
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lech_Walesa" title="Lech Walesa">
       Lech Walesa
      </a>
      and alliances such as the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Solidarity_Movement" title="Solidarity Movement">
       Solidarity Movement
      </a>
      . Poland and Czechoslovakia would achieve independence in 1989, and East Germany(from the Soviet sphere of influence) and Estonia in 1991. Other nations such as Ukraine would not achieve independence until the collapse of the Soviet Union on December 26, 1991.
     </p>
     <div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article:
      <a href="/wiki/Wars_of_national_liberation" title="Wars of national liberation">
       Wars of national liberation
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      The Soviet Union sought to effect the abolishment of colonial governance by Western countries and replace it with the rule of a local
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Communist_Party" title="Communist Party">
       Communist Party
      </a>
      under the influence of the Soviet Union, either by direct subversion of Western-leaning or -controlled governments or indirectly by influence of political leadership and support. Many of the revolutions and civil war of this time period were inspired or influenced in this way. The conflicts in Vietnam,
      <a href="/wiki/Nicaragua" title="Nicaragua">
       Nicaragua
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Democratic Republic of the Congo">
       Congo
      </a>
      , and
      <a href="/wiki/Sudan" title="Sudan">
       Sudan
      </a>
      , among others, have been characterized as such.
     </p>
     <p>
      Most Soviet leaders expressed the
      <a href="/wiki/Leninism" title="Leninism">
       MarxistLeninist
      </a>
      view that
      <a href="/wiki/Imperialism" title="Imperialism">
       imperialism
      </a>
      was the height of
      <a href="/wiki/Capitalism" title="Capitalism">
       capitalism
      </a>
      , and generated a class-stratified society. It followed, then, that Soviet leadership would encourage independence movements in colonized territories, especially as the
      <a href="/wiki/Cold_War" title="Cold War">
       Cold War
      </a>
      progressed. Though this was the view expressed by their leaders, such interventions can be interpreted
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Words_to_watch#Unsupported_attributions" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Words to watch">
         <span title="The material near this tag possibly uses too-vague attribution or weasel words. (December 2010)">
          who?
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
      as the expansion of Soviet interests, not just as aiding the oppressed peoples of the world. Because so many of these wars of independence expanded into general Cold War conflicts, the United States also supported several such independence movements in opposition to Soviet interests.
     </p>
     <p>
      <a href="/wiki/Nikita_Khrushchev" title="Nikita Khrushchev">
       Nikita Khrushchev
      </a>
      's famous
      <a href="/wiki/Shoe-banging_incident" title="Shoe-banging incident">
       shoe-banging incident
      </a>
      occurred in the context of a
      <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">
       United Nations
      </a>
      debate on colonialism in 1960. After Khrushchev had decried western colonialism, Filipino delegate
      <a href="/wiki/Lorenzo_Sumulong" title="Lorenzo Sumulong">
       Lorenzo Sumulong
      </a>
      accused him of hypocrisy, claiming that the Soviet Union was at that time doing exactly the same thing to the countries of
      <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Europe" title="Eastern Europe">
       Eastern Europe
      </a>
      . Khrushchev then reportedly became enraged and theatrically banged his shoe on the table while berating Sumulong as a "toady of imperialism," though accounts of the incident differ.
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Decolonization_after_1945">
       Decolonization after 1945
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Decolonization&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Decolonization after 1945">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <h4>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="The_emergence_of_the_Third_World_.281945.E2.80.93.29">
       The emergence of the Third World (1945)
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Decolonization&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: The emergence of the Third World (1945)">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h4>
     <div class="hatnote">
      See also:
      <a href="/wiki/Decolonization_of_Africa" title="Decolonization of Africa">
       Decolonization of Africa
      </a>
     </div>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Africa_cs_poster.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="325" data-file-width="239" height="272" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/8/85/Africa_cs_poster.jpg/200px-Africa_cs_poster.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/8/85/Africa_cs_poster.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/8/85/Africa_cs_poster.jpg 2x" width="200"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Africa_cs_poster.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Czechoslovak anti-colonialist propaganda poster: "Africa - in fight for freedom".
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      The term "
      <a href="/wiki/Third_World" title="Third World">
       Third World
      </a>
      " was coined by French demographer
      <a href="/wiki/Alfred_Sauvy" title="Alfred Sauvy">
       Alfred Sauvy
      </a>
      in 1952, on the model of the
      <a href="/wiki/Estates_General_(France)" title="Estates General (France)">
       Third Estate
      </a>
      , which, according to the
      <a href="/wiki/Emmanuel_Joseph_Siey%C3%A8s" title="Emmanuel Joseph Sieys">
       Abb Sieys
      </a>
      , represented everything, but was nothing: "...because at the end this ignored, exploited, scorned Third World like the Third Estate, wants to become something too" (Sauvy). The emergence of this new political entity, in the frame of the
      <a href="/wiki/Cold_War" title="Cold War">
       Cold War
      </a>
      , was complex and painful. Several tentatives were made to organize newly independent states in order to oppose a common front towards both the US's and the USSR's influence on them, with the consequences of the
      <a href="/wiki/Sino-Soviet_split" title="Sino-Soviet split">
       Sino-Soviet split
      </a>
      already at works. Thus, the
      <a href="/wiki/Non-Aligned_Movement" title="Non-Aligned Movement">
       Non-Aligned Movement
      </a>
      constituted itself, around the main figures of
      <a href="/wiki/Jawaharlal_Nehru" title="Jawaharlal Nehru">
       Jawaharlal Nehru
      </a>
      , the leader of India,
      <a href="/wiki/Sukarno" title="Sukarno">
       Sukarno
      </a>
      , the Indonesian president,
      <a href="/wiki/Josip_Broz_Tito" title="Josip Broz Tito">
       Josip Broz Tito
      </a>
      the Communist leader of
      <a href="/wiki/Socialist_Federal_Republic_of_Yugoslavia" title="Socialist Federal Republic of Yugoslavia">
       Yugoslavia
      </a>
      , and
      <a href="/wiki/Gamal_Abdel_Nasser" title="Gamal Abdel Nasser">
       Gamal Abdel Nasser
      </a>
      , head of Egypt who successfully opposed the French and British imperial powers during the 1956
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Suez_crisis" title="Suez crisis">
       Suez crisis
      </a>
      . After the 1954
      <a href="/wiki/Geneva_Conference_(1954)" title="Geneva Conference (1954)">
       Geneva Conference
      </a>
      which put an end to the
      <a href="/wiki/First_Indochina_War" title="First Indochina War">
       First Indochina War
      </a>
      , the 1955
      <a href="/wiki/Bandung_Conference" title="Bandung Conference">
       Bandung Conference
      </a>
      gathered Nasser, Nehru, Tito,
      <a href="/wiki/Sukarno" title="Sukarno">
       Sukarno
      </a>
      , the leader of Indonesia, and
      <a href="/wiki/Zhou_Enlai" title="Zhou Enlai">
       Zhou Enlai
      </a>
      ,
      <a href="/wiki/Premier_of_the_People%27s_Republic_of_China" title="Premier of the People's Republic of China">
       Premier of the People's Republic of China
      </a>
      . In 1960, the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UN_General_Assembly" title="UN General Assembly">
       UN General Assembly
      </a>
      voted the
      <a href="/wiki/Declaration_on_the_Granting_of_Independence_to_Colonial_Countries_and_Peoples" title="Declaration on the Granting of Independence to Colonial Countries and Peoples">
       Declaration on the Granting of Independence to Colonial Countries and Peoples
      </a>
      . The next year, the Non-Aligned Movement was officially created in
      <a href="/wiki/Belgrade" title="Belgrade">
       Belgrade
      </a>
      (1961), and was followed in 1964 by the creation of the
      <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Conference_on_Trade_and_Development" title="United Nations Conference on Trade and Development">
       United Nations Conference on Trade and Development
      </a>
      (UNCTAD) which tried to promote a
      <a href="/wiki/New_International_Economic_Order" title="New International Economic Order">
       New International Economic Order
      </a>
      (NIEO). The NIEO was opposed to the 1944
      <a href="/wiki/Bretton_Woods_system" title="Bretton Woods system">
       Bretton Woods system
      </a>
      , which had benefited the leading states which had created it, and remained in force until 1971 after the United States' suspension of convertibility from dollars to gold. The main tenets of the NIEO were:
     </p>
     <ol>
      <li>
       Developing countries must be entitled to regulate and control the activities of
       <a href="/wiki/Multinational_corporation" title="Multinational corporation">
        multinational corporations
       </a>
       operating within their territory.
      </li>
      <li>
       They must be free to
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nationalize" title="Nationalize">
        nationalize
       </a>
       or
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Expropriate" title="Expropriate">
        expropriate
       </a>
       foreign property on conditions favourable to them.
      </li>
      <li>
       They must be free to set up associations of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Primary_commodities" title="Primary commodities">
        primary commodities
       </a>
       producers similar to the
       <a href="/wiki/OPEC" title="OPEC">
        Organization of the Petroleum Exporting Countries
       </a>
       , created on September 17, 1960 to protest pressure by major oil companies (mostly owned by U.S., British, and Dutch nationals) to reduce oil prices and payments to producers); all other states must recognize this right and refrain from taking economic, military, or political measures calculated to restrict it.
      </li>
      <li>
       International trade should be based on the need to ensure stable, equitable, and remunerative prices for raw materials, generalized non-reciprocal and non-discriminatory tariff preferences, as well as
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Transfer_of_technology" title="Transfer of technology">
        transfer of technology
       </a>
       to developing countries; and should provide economic and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Technical_assistance" title="Technical assistance">
        technical assistance
       </a>
       without any
       <a href="/wiki/Conditionality" title="Conditionality">
        strings attached
       </a>
       .
      </li>
     </ol>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:352px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:HDImap_current.png">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="625" data-file-width="1350" height="162" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/HDImap_current.png/350px-HDImap_current.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/HDImap_current.png/525px-HDImap_current.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/HDImap_current.png/700px-HDImap_current.png 2x" width="350"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:HDImap_current.png" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        The
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UN_Human_Development_Index" title="UN Human Development Index">
         UN Human Development Index
        </a>
        (HDI) is a quantitative index of development, alternative to the classic
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gross_Domestic_Product" title="Gross Domestic Product">
         Gross Domestic Product
        </a>
        (GDP), which some use as a proxy to define the
        <a href="/wiki/Third_World" title="Third World">
         Third World
        </a>
        . While the GDP only calculates economic wealth, the HDI includes
        <a href="/wiki/Life_expectancy" title="Life expectancy">
         life expectancy
        </a>
        ,
        <a href="/wiki/Public_health" title="Public health">
         public health
        </a>
        and
        <a href="/wiki/Literacy" title="Literacy">
         literacy
        </a>
        as fundamental factors of a good
        <a href="/wiki/Quality_of_life" title="Quality of life">
         quality of life
        </a>
        .
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      The UNCTAD however wasn't very effective in implementing this New International Economic Order (NIEO), and social and economic inequalities between industrialized countries and the Third World kept on growing throughout the 1960s until the 21st century. The
      <a href="/wiki/1973_oil_crisis" title="1973 oil crisis">
       1973 oil crisis
      </a>
      which followed the
      <a href="/wiki/Yom_Kippur_War" title="Yom Kippur War">
       Yom Kippur War
      </a>
      (October 1973) was triggered by the OPEC which decided an embargo against the US and Western countries, causing a fourfold increase in the price of oil, which lasted five months, starting on October 17, 1973, and ending on March 18, 1974. OPEC nations then agreed, on January 7, 1975, to raise crude oil prices by 10%. At that time, OPEC nationsincluding many who had recently nationalised their oil industriesjoined the call for a New International Economic Order to be initiated by coalitions of primary producers. Concluding the First OPEC Summit in Algiers they called for stable and just commodity prices, an international food and agriculture program, technology transfer from North to South, and the democratization of the economic system. But industrialized countries quickly began to look for substitutes to OPEC petroleum, with the oil companies investing the majority of their research capital in the US and European countries or others, politically sure countries. The OPEC lost more and more influence on the world prices of oil.
     </p>
     <p>
      The
      <a href="/wiki/1979_energy_crisis" title="1979 energy crisis">
       second oil crisis
      </a>
      occurred in the wake of the 1979
      <a href="/wiki/Iranian_Revolution" title="Iranian Revolution">
       Iranian Revolution
      </a>
      . Then, the 1982
      <a href="/wiki/Latin_American_debt_crisis" title="Latin American debt crisis">
       Latin American debt crisis
      </a>
      exploded in Mexico first, then Argentina and Brazil, which proved unable to pay back their debts, jeopardizing the existence of the international economic system.
     </p>
     <p>
      The 1990s were characterized by the prevalence of the
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Washington_consensus" title="Washington consensus">
       Washington consensus
      </a>
      on
      <a href="/wiki/Neoliberalism" title="Neoliberalism">
       neoliberal
      </a>
      policies, "
      <a href="/wiki/Structural_adjustment" title="Structural adjustment">
       structural adjustment
      </a>
      " and "
      <a href="/wiki/Shock_therapy_(economics)" title="Shock therapy (economics)">
       shock therapies
      </a>
      " for the former Communist states.
     </p>
     <h4>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Decolonization_in_the_Americas_after_1945">
       Decolonization in the Americas after 1945
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Decolonization&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Decolonization in the Americas after 1945">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h4>
     <ul>
      <li>
       <span class="flagicon">
        <img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="1200" height="12" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/ae/Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg/23px-Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/ae/Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg/35px-Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/ae/Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg/46px-Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg.png 2x" width="23"/>
       </span>
       <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">
        United Kingdom
       </a>
       :
       <a href="/wiki/Dominion_of_Newfoundland" title="Dominion of Newfoundland">
        Newfoundland
       </a>
       (nominally an independent dominion but under direct British rule since 1934) (1949, union with Canada);
       <a href="/wiki/Guyana" title="Guyana">
        Guyana
       </a>
       (1966);
       <a href="/wiki/Belize" title="Belize">
        Belize
       </a>
       (1981).
      </li>
      <li>
       <span class="flagicon">
        <img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="900" height="15" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/Flag_of_the_Netherlands.svg/23px-Flag_of_the_Netherlands.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/Flag_of_the_Netherlands.svg/35px-Flag_of_the_Netherlands.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/Flag_of_the_Netherlands.svg/45px-Flag_of_the_Netherlands.svg.png 2x" width="23"/>
       </span>
       <a href="/wiki/Netherlands" title="Netherlands">
        Netherlands
       </a>
       :
       <a href="/wiki/Netherlands_Antilles" title="Netherlands Antilles">
        Netherlands Antilles
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Suriname" title="Suriname">
        Suriname
       </a>
       (1954, both becoming constituent countries of the
       <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_the_Netherlands" title="Kingdom of the Netherlands">
        Kingdom of the Netherlands
       </a>
       ).
      </li>
      <li>
       <span class="flagicon">
        <img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="280" data-file-width="370" height="15" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Flag_of_Denmark.svg/20px-Flag_of_Denmark.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Flag_of_Denmark.svg/31px-Flag_of_Denmark.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Flag_of_Denmark.svg/40px-Flag_of_Denmark.svg.png 2x" width="20"/>
       </span>
       <a href="/wiki/Denmark" title="Denmark">
        Denmark
       </a>
       :
       <a href="/wiki/Greenland" title="Greenland">
        Greenland
       </a>
       (1979, became a constituent country of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Denmark" title="Kingdom of Denmark">
        Kingdom of Denmark
       </a>
       ).
      </li>
     </ul>
     <h4>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Decolonization_of_Asia">
       Decolonization of Asia
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Decolonization&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Decolonization of Asia">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h4>
     <div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article:
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Decolonization_of_Asia" title="Decolonization of Asia">
       Decolonization of Asia
      </a>
     </div>
     <table class="metadata plainlinks ambox mbox-small-left ambox-content" role="presentation">
      <tr>
       <td class="mbox-image">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg">
         <img alt="[icon]" data-file-height="31" data-file-width="44" height="14" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/20px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/30px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/40px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png 2x" width="20"/>
        </a>
       </td>
       <td class="mbox-text">
        <span class="mbox-text-span">
         This section requires
         <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Decolonization&amp;action=edit">
          expansion
         </a>
         .
         <small>
          <i>
           (August 2010)
          </i>
         </small>
        </span>
       </td>
      </tr>
     </table>
     <p>
      The following list shows the colonial powers following the end of hostilities in 1945, and their colonial or administrative possessions. The year of decolonization is given chronologically in parentheses.
     </p>
     <ul>
      <li>
       <span class="flagicon">
        <img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="1200" height="12" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/ae/Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg/23px-Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/ae/Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg/35px-Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/a/ae/Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg/46px-Flag_of_the_United_Kingdom.svg.png 2x" width="23"/>
       </span>
       <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">
        United Kingdom
       </a>
       :
       <a href="/wiki/Presidencies_and_provinces_of_British_India" title="Presidencies and provinces of British India">
        British India
       </a>
       (1947);
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/British_Mandate_of_Palestine" title="British Mandate of Palestine">
        British Mandate of Palestine
       </a>
       , Burma, and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ceylon" title="Ceylon">
        Ceylon
       </a>
       (1948);
       <a href="/wiki/British_Malaya" title="British Malaya">
        British Malaya
       </a>
       (1957);
       <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Sarawak" title="Kingdom of Sarawak">
        Kingdom of Sarawak
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/North_Borneo" title="North Borneo">
        North Borneo
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Singapore" title="Singapore">
        Singapore
       </a>
       (1963);
       <a href="/wiki/Brunei" title="Brunei">
        Brunei
       </a>
       (1984);
       <a href="/wiki/Hong_Kong" title="Hong Kong">
        Hong Kong
       </a>
       (1997).
      </li>
      <li>
       <span class="flagicon">
        <img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="900" height="15" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/c3/Flag_of_France.svg/23px-Flag_of_France.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/c3/Flag_of_France.svg/35px-Flag_of_France.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/c3/Flag_of_France.svg/45px-Flag_of_France.svg.png 2x" width="23"/>
       </span>
       <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">
        France
       </a>
       :
       <a href="/wiki/French_India" title="French India">
        French India
       </a>
       (1954) and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Indochina" title="Indochina">
        Indochina
       </a>
       (comprising Vietnam (1945),
       <a href="/wiki/Cambodia" title="Cambodia">
        Cambodia
       </a>
       (1953) and
       <a href="/wiki/Laos" title="Laos">
        Laos
       </a>
       ).
      </li>
      <li>
       <span class="flagicon">
        <img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="400" data-file-width="600" height="15" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Flag_of_Portugal.svg/23px-Flag_of_Portugal.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Flag_of_Portugal.svg/35px-Flag_of_Portugal.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5c/Flag_of_Portugal.svg/45px-Flag_of_Portugal.svg.png 2x" width="23"/>
       </span>
       <a href="/wiki/Portugal" title="Portugal">
        Portugal
       </a>
       :
       <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_India" title="Portuguese India">

       (1961);
       <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Timor" title="Portuguese Timor">

       </a>
       (1975);

       </span>

       (1946): Philippines

       </span>

     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Assassinated_anticolonialist_leaders">
       Assassinated anticolonialist leaders
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Decolonization&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Assassinated anticolonialist leaders">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Gandhi_with_Lord_and_Lady_Mountbatten_1947.jpg">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="375" data-file-width="543" height="152" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Gandhi_with_Lord_and_Lady_Mountbatten_1947.jpg/220px-Gandhi_with_Lord_and_Lady_Mountbatten_1947.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Gandhi_with_Lord_and_Lady_Mountbatten_1947.jpg/330px-Gandhi_with_Lord_and_Lady_Mountbatten_1947.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Gandhi_with_Lord_and_Lady_Mountbatten_1947.jpg/440px-Gandhi_with_Lord_and_Lady_Mountbatten_1947.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Gandhi_with_Lord_and_Lady_Mountbatten_1947.jpg" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Gandhi in 1947, with Lord
        <a href="/wiki/Louis_Mountbatten,_1st_Earl_Mountbatten_of_Burma" title="Louis Mountbatten, 1st Earl Mountbatten of Burma">
         Louis Mountbatten
        </a>
        , Britain's last Viceroy of India, and his wife Vicereine
        <a href="/wiki/Edwina_Mountbatten,_Countess_Mountbatten_of_Burma" title="Edwina Mountbatten, Countess Mountbatten of Burma">
         Edwina Mountbatten
        </a>
        .
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      A
      <i>
       non-exhaustive
      </i>
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_assassinated_people" title="List of assassinated people">
       list of assassinated leaders
      </a>
      would include:
     </p>
     <ul>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/Tiradentes" title="Tiradentes">
        Tiradentes
       </a>
       was a leading member of the Brazilian seditious movement known as the
       <a href="/wiki/Inconfid%C3%AAncia_Mineira" title="Inconfidncia Mineira">
        Inconfidncia Mineira
       </a>
       , against the
       <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Empire" title="Portuguese Empire">
        Portuguese Empire
       </a>
       . He fought for an independent Brazilian republic.
      </li>
      <li>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mohandas_Karamchand_Gandhi" title="Mohandas Karamchand Gandhi">
        Mohandas Karamchand Gandhi
       </a>
       , nonviolent leader of the
       <a href="/wiki/Indian_independence_movement" title="Indian independence movement">
        Indian independence movement
       </a>
       was assassinated in 1948 by Hindu extremists.
      </li>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/Ruben_Um_Nyob%C3%A9" title="Ruben Um Nyob">
        Ruben Um Nyob
       </a>
       , leader of the
       <a href="/wiki/Union_of_the_Peoples_of_Cameroon" title="Union of the Peoples of Cameroon">
        Union of the Peoples of Cameroon
       </a>
       (UPC), killed by the French
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/SDECE" title="SDECE">
        SDECE
       </a>
       on September 13, 1958. No clear cause has ever been ascertained for the mysterious crash. Assassination has been alleged.
      </li>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/Barth%C3%A9lemy_Boganda" title="Barthlemy Boganda">
        Barthlemy Boganda
       </a>
       , leader of a nationalist
       <a href="/wiki/Central_African_Republic" title="Central African Republic">
        Central African Republic
       </a>
       movement, who died in a plane-crash on March 29, 1959, eight days before the last elections of the colonial era.
      </li>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/F%C3%A9lix-Roland_Moumi%C3%A9" title="Flix-Roland Moumi">
        Flix-Roland Moumi
       </a>
       , successor to Ruben Um Nyobe at the head of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cameroon%27s_People_Union" title="Cameroon's People Union">
        Cameroon's People Union
       </a>
       , assassinated in
       <a href="/wiki/Geneva" title="Geneva">
        Geneva
       </a>
       in 1960 by the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/SDECE" title="SDECE">
        SDECE
       </a>
       (French secret services).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22">
        <a href="#cite_note-22">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         22
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </li>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/Patrice_Lumumba" title="Patrice Lumumba">
        Patrice Lumumba
       </a>
       , the first Prime Minister of the
       <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Democratic Republic of the Congo">
        Democratic Republic of the Congo
       </a>
       , was assassinated on January 17, 1961.
      </li>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/Burundi" title="Burundi">
        Burundi
       </a>
       nationalist
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Louis_Rwagasore" title="Louis Rwagasore">
        Louis Rwagasore
       </a>
       was assassinated on October 13, 1961, while
       <a href="/wiki/Pierre_Ngendandumwe" title="Pierre Ngendandumwe">
        Pierre Ngendandumwe
       </a>
       , Burundi's first
       <a href="/wiki/Hutu" title="Hutu">
        Hutu
       </a>
       prime minister, was also murdered on January 15, 1965.
      </li>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/Sylvanus_Olympio" title="Sylvanus Olympio">
        Sylvanus Olympio
       </a>
       , the first
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_Presidents_of_Togo" title="List of Presidents of Togo">
        president of Togo
       </a>
       , was assassinated on January 13, 1963.
      </li>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/Mehdi_Ben_Barka" title="Mehdi Ben Barka">
        Mehdi Ben Barka
       </a>
       , the leader of the
       <a href="/wiki/History_of_Morocco" title="History of Morocco">
        Moroccan
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/National_Union_of_Popular_Forces" title="National Union of Popular Forces">
        National Union of Popular Forces
       </a>
       (UNPF) and of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tricontinental_Conference" title="Tricontinental Conference">
        Tricontinental Conference
       </a>
       , which was supposed to prepare in 1966 in
       <a href="/wiki/Havana" title="Havana">
        Havana
       </a>
       its first meeting gathering national liberation movements from all continents  related to the
       <a href="/wiki/Non-Aligned_Movement" title="Non-Aligned Movement">
        Non-Aligned Movement
       </a>
       , but the Tricontinal Conference gathered liberation movements while the Non-Aligned were for the most part states  was "
       <a href="/wiki/Forced_disappearance" title="Forced disappearance">
        disappeared
       </a>
       " in Paris in 1965, allegedly by Moroccan agents and French
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Police_officers" title="Police officers">
        police officers
       </a>
       .
      </li>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/Nigeria" title="Nigeria">
        Nigerian
       </a>
       leader
       <a href="/wiki/Ahmadu_Bello" title="Ahmadu Bello">
        Ahmadu Bello
       </a>
       was assassinated in January 1966 during a coup which toppled Nigeria's post-independence government.
      </li>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/Eduardo_Mondlane" title="Eduardo Mondlane">
        Eduardo Mondlane
       </a>
       , the leader of
       <a href="/wiki/FRELIMO" title="FRELIMO">
        FRELIMO
       </a>
       and the father of
       <a href="/wiki/Mozambique" title="Mozambique">
        Mozambican
       </a>
       independence, was assassinated in 1969. Both the Portuguese intelligence or the Portuguese secret police PIDE/DGS and elements of FRELIMO, have been accused of killing Mondlane.
      </li>
      <li>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mohamed_Bassiri" title="Mohamed Bassiri">
        Mohamed Bassiri
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Sahrawi_people" title="Sahrawi people">
        Sahrawi
       </a>
       leader of the
       <a href="/wiki/Movement_for_the_Liberation_of_Saguia_el_Hamra_and_Wadi_el_Dhahab" title="Movement for the Liberation of Saguia el Hamra and Wadi el Dhahab">
        Movement for the Liberation of Saguia el Hamra and Wadi el Dhahab
       </a>
       was "disappeared" in
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/El_Aai%C3%BAn" title="El Aain">
        El Aain
       </a>
       in 1970, allegedly by the
       <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Legion" title="Spanish Legion">
        Spanish Legion
       </a>
       .
      </li>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/Am%C3%ADlcar_Cabral" title="Amlcar Cabral">
        Amlcar Cabral
       </a>
       was killed on January 20, 1973 by PAIGC rival Inocncio Kani, with the help of Portuguese agents operating within the PAIGC.
      </li>
     </ul>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Post-colonial_organizations">
       Post-colonial organizations
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Decolonization&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Post-colonial organizations">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <div class="thumb tright">
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:402px;">
       <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Postempire_Orgs_Map.png">
        <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="628" data-file-width="1357" height="185" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Postempire_Orgs_Map.png/400px-Postempire_Orgs_Map.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Postempire_Orgs_Map.png/600px-Postempire_Orgs_Map.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Postempire_Orgs_Map.png/800px-Postempire_Orgs_Map.png 2x" width="400"/>
       </a>
       <div class="thumbcaption">
        <div class="magnify">
         <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Postempire_Orgs_Map.png" title="Enlarge">
         </a>
        </div>
        Four international organizations whose membership largely follows the pattern of previous colonial empires.
       </div>
      </div>
     </div>
     <p>
      Due to a common history and culture, former colonial powers created institutions which more loosely associated their former colonies. Membership is voluntary, and in some cases can be revoked if a member state loses some objective criteria (usually a requirement for democratic governance). The organizations serve cultural, economic, and political purposes between the associated countries, although no such organization has become politically prominent as an entity in its own right.
     </p>
     <table class="wikitable">
      <tr style="background-color:#e9e9e9">
       <th>
        Former Colonial Power
       </th>

        Organization
       </th>

        Founded
       </th>
      </tr>

         Commonwealth of Nations

       </td>

        <i>

     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Differing_perspectives">
       Differing perspectives
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Decolonization&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Differing perspectives">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <table class="metadata plainlinks ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation">
      <tr>
       <td class="mbox-image">
        <div style="width:52px">
         <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg">
          <img alt="" data-file-height="204" data-file-width="262" height="39" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" width="50"/>
         </a>
        </div>
       </td>
       <td class="mbox-text">
        <span class="mbox-text-span">
         This article
         <b>
          needs additional citations for
          <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">
           verification
          </a>
         </b>
         .
         <span class="hide-when-compact">
          Please help
          <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Decolonization&amp;action=edit">
           improve this article
          </a>
          by
          <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing/1">
           adding citations to reliable sources
          </a>
          . Unsourced material may be challenged and removed.
         </span>
         <small>
          <i>
           (November 2008)
          </i>
         </small>
        </span>
       </td>
      </tr>
     </table>
     <p>
      There is quite a bit of controversy over decolonisation. The end goal tends to be universally regarded as good, but there has been much debate over the best way to grant full independence.
     </p>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Economic_effects">
       Economic effects
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Decolonization&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Economic effects">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <h4>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Effects_on_the_colonizers">
       Effects on the colonizers
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Decolonization&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Effects on the colonizers">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h4>
     <p>
      <a href="/wiki/John_Kenneth_Galbraith" title="John Kenneth Galbraith">
       John Kenneth Galbraith
      </a>
      argues that the postWorld War II decolonization was brought about for economic reasons. In
      <i>
       A Journey Through Economic Time
      </i>
      , he writes:
     </p>
     <blockquote>
      <p>
       "The engine of economic well-being was now within and between the advanced industrial countries. Domestic
       <a href="/wiki/Economic_growth" title="Economic growth">
        economic growth
       </a>
        as now measured and much discussed  came to be seen as far more important than the erstwhile colonial trade.... The economic effect in the United States from the granting of independence to the Philippines was unnoticeable, partly due to the
       <a href="/wiki/Bell_Trade_Act" title="Bell Trade Act">
        Bell Trade Act
       </a>
       , which allowed American monopoly in the economy of the Philippines. The departure of India and Pakistan made small economic difference in the United Kingdom.
       <a href="/wiki/Netherlands" title="Netherlands">
        Dutch
       </a>
       economists calculated that the economic effect from the loss of the great Dutch empire in Indonesia was compensated for by a couple of years or so of domestic post-war economic growth. The end of the colonial era is celebrated in the history books as a triumph of national aspiration in the former colonies and of benign good sense on the part of the colonial powers. Lurking beneath, as so often happens, was a strong current of economic interest  or in this case, disinterest."
      </p>
     </blockquote>
     <p>
      In general, the release of the colonized caused little economic loss to the colonizers. Part of the reason for this was that major costs were eliminated while major benefits were obtained by alternate means. Decolonization allowed the colonizer to disclaim responsibility for the colonized. The colonizer no longer had the burden of obligation, financial or otherwise, to their colony. However, the colonizer continued to be able to obtain cheap goods and labor as well as economic benefits (see
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Suez_Canal_Crisis" title="Suez Canal Crisis">
       Suez Canal Crisis
      </a>
      ) from the former colonies. Financial, political and military pressure could still be used to achieve goals desired by the colonizer. Thus decolonization allowed the goals of colonization to be largely achieved, but without its burdens.
     </p>
     <h4>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Effects_on_the_former_colonies">
       Effects on the former colonies
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Decolonization&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Effects on the former colonies">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h4>
     <div class="hatnote">
      Further information:
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Third_World_debt" title="Third World debt">
       Third World debt
      </a>
     </div>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Settled_populations">
       Settled populations
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Decolonization&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Settled populations">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <p>
      Decolonization is not an easy matter in colonies where a large population of settlers lives, particularly if they have been there for several generations. This population, in general, may have to be repatriated, often losing considerable property. For instance, the decolonisation of
      <a href="/wiki/Algeria" title="Algeria">
       Algeria
      </a>
      by France was particularly uneasy due to the large European and Sephardic Jewish population (see also
      <i>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pied_noir" title="Pied noir">
        pied noir
       </a>
      </i>
      ), which largely evacuated to France when Algeria became independent. In
      <a href="/wiki/Zimbabwe" title="Zimbabwe">
       Zimbabwe
      </a>
      , former
      <a href="/wiki/Rhodesia" title="Rhodesia">
       Rhodesia
      </a>
      , president
      <a href="/wiki/Robert_Mugabe" title="Robert Mugabe">
       Robert Mugabe
      </a>
      has, starting in the 1990s, targeted
      <a href="/wiki/White_Africans_of_European_ancestry" title="White Africans of European ancestry">
       white African farmers
      </a>
      and forcibly seized their property. In some cases, decolonisation is hardly possible or impossible because of the importance of the settler population or where the indigenous population is now in the minority; such is the case of the British population of the
      <a href="/wiki/Cayman_Islands" title="Cayman Islands">
       Cayman Islands
      </a>
      .
      <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
       [
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
         <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2014)">
          citation needed
         </span>
        </a>
       </i>
       ]
      </sup>
     </p>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Timeline_of_independence">
       Timeline of independence
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=Decolonization&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Timeline of independence">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <div class="hatnote">
      Further information:
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_national_independence_days" title="List of national independence days">
       List of national independence days
      </a>
     </div>
     <p>
      This list includes formerly non-self-governing territories, such as colonies, protectorates,
      <a href="/wiki/Condominium_(international_law)" title="Condominium (international law)">
       condominia
      </a>
      , and leased territories. Changes in status of autonomy leading up to and after independence are not listed, and some dates of independence may be disputed. For details, see each national history.
     </p>
